Britain's Policy Towards Germany Changes, Facilitating Resolution of the Far East Situation 52

Amsterdam The Dutch newspapers generally view the conclusion of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement as a victory for German diplomacy. The Dutch Daily commented that Britain, feeling it was more advantageous to deal directly with Germany, had abandoned the policy of appeasement. This sudden change in attitude is probably due to the difficulties Britain has encountered in its naval policy in Europe, which are not as concerning as those in the Far East, forcing Britain to resolve one issue first and shift its attention to the other. Moreover, in recent days, the situation in the Far East has become extremely tense. To protect the interests of the British Empire, Britain necessarily needs to resolve the European problem quickly. Therefore, from this point of view, Britain's change of attitude is very beneficial to the Netherlands, as the Netherlands also has pressing interests in the Far East. A Berlin correspondent for the Telegraph reported that Germany's international isolation is now a thing of the past. Germany's diplomatic victory is the result of Hitler's speech to the Reichstag making a good impression on Britain, and also the success of his advocacy of bilateral agreements to maintain a balanced policy. The People's Daily said that the question now is how Laval can recognize the current situation, seize the opportunity, and reach a compromise with Germany. (20th National News Agency)

First Voice of Diplomatic Victory, German Newspapers Comment with Pride and Satisfaction 53

(Berlin) Viewed from the perspective of the overall resolution of the European problem, and the only effective method of resolving it, the significance of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement is by no means limited to the benefits enjoyed by the signatory countries. This is what the Diplomatic and Political Review hints is the opinion of the German authorities. The newspaper also stated that it is particularly noteworthy that by using the method of free negotiation, the interests and defense of both countries are taken into account, and concrete disarmament is realized. Britain's maritime hegemony and Germany's naval protection of its coasts and the freedom to maintain traffic in its ports have been recognized. (19th National News Agency)

Britain differs from France in that it not only recognizes Germany's claimed equal rights in principle, but also fulfills its promise. (20th National Telegram)

Attention of Japanese Naval Circles 55

(Tokyo) Japanese naval circles are now paying close attention to the Anglo-German Naval Agreement. It is evident that the United States still firmly adheres to the ratio method and classification restrictions. However, the newspaper stated that various countries now have strong objections to this method of restriction, fearing that France may confront Germany, leading to a naval arms race. (20th Reuters)

(Tokyo) The contents of the naval agreement concluded between the British and German governments were announced on the 18th. At the same time, the British Foreign Office sent it to Japanese Ambassador Matsudaira, requesting that it be transmitted to the Japanese government. The Japanese Foreign Ministry maintains the following view on the conclusion of the agreement: The Anglo-German Naval Agreement is a local European issue, and the 35% figure does not strengthen ratioism. Britain is attempting to use this local ratioism to limit the world's navies. We should pay close attention to its attitude with caution. The upcoming Anglo-French naval conference is also a European issue, but its importance is many times greater than the Anglo-German conference. The Anglo-German 35% ratioism has a great impact on the strength of French and German capital ships. France will definitely not acquiesce to this agreement. It is not difficult to imagine that Britain and France will compromise, and France will expand its navy. There is no need to elaborate on the impact this will have on the world's naval disarmament issue. (20th Domei News Agency)

British Farewell to Matsudaira, Speech on Anglo-Japanese Relations 58

(London) Australian High Commissioner Bruce hosted a banquet today to bid farewell to Japanese Ambassador to Britain Matsudaira. British Foreign Secretary Hoare also attended the banquet. During the banquet, Bruce spoke, stating that in today's world, nothing deserves more attention than the Pacific, and the occurrence of various major problems in the future is likely to be in the Pacific. Therefore, he advocated that good relations should be maintained between Britain and Japan, and he deeply believed that the peace of the Pacific would depend on the relationship between Britain and Japan. After finishing his speech, British Foreign Secretary Hoare rose and deeply praised the maintenance of close relations between Britain and Japan, while acknowledging that there were indeed some difficulties. For example, the news coming from North China today is somewhat of an example of causing unease in the relations between the two countries. Finally, Matsudaira stood up and replied, stating that the good relationship between Britain and Japan has not been established in just one day. In recent years, due to various problems, the two countries have inevitably had misunderstandings and suspicions, but if sincerity and understanding can be shown, then any problem will be resolved sooner or later. (19th National News Agency)

(London) Japanese Ambassador to Britain Matsudaira will return to Japan in a few days. The Japanese Association held a special banquet tonight to bid farewell to Matsudaira and his wife. British Foreign Secretary Hoare was also one of the guests and gave a speech, saying that Britain views a just understanding and cooperation with Japan as an important means of ensuring the security of Asia and the prosperity of the world. He hoped that Matsudaira would tell his compatriots when he and his wife returned to their country, with the announcement of the British people, "We deeply know that we now have many things that are related to most of the world. We are both large island nations and still enjoy the unparalleled blessings of traditional monarchs. We are both brave nations and will leave our mark on the history of the world. If there are any difficulties, let us discuss them like friends who are eager to understand each other's opinions." The relationship between Britain and Japan, in recent times, has not been entirely free of disturbing factors. I will now only mention the information we have received from North China, and the difficulties that the two major industrial countries may encounter in conducting business in the world at any time. I hope Your Excellency will tell your countrymen that many men and women in Britain wish to see these difficulties eliminated. We dare to say that many men and women in Japan share this feeling. Matsudaira replied that the friendship between Britain and Japan has stood the test of time and remains as firm as tradition. In recent years, several problems have caused misunderstandings and unhappiness between us, but there are no difficult problems that cannot be resolved sooner or later with mutual goodwill and sincerity. Today, not only the Far East is unstable, but the whole world also presents this picture. This is indeed regrettable. Now, greater efforts are needed to eliminate misunderstandings between countries. This goal cannot be achieved solely through the efforts of diplomats and officials. Direct contact between countries is also necessary. Matsudaira further said that the International Cultural Association is currently discussing sending a university professor to Britain to lecture on Japanese art. He felt that a good understanding and friendship between Britain and Japan is essential to peace in the Far East. We must continue to make sincere efforts to seek this peace. Australian High Commissioner to London Bruce then declared that the place where the biggest problems in the world will occur in the future is probably in the Pacific, so a very happy understanding and harmonious relationship between Britain and Japan is essential. (19th Reuters)

Belgian War Veterans Oppose, Franco-Belgian Military Alliance, Advocate Adopting a Policy of Voluntary Neutrality, Peace Guarantee Must Rely on National Understanding 59

Brussels The president of the Association of Flemish War Veterans in Belgium issued a declaration to the Belgian and foreign press, opposing recent pro-French remarks in Belgium, stating that peace cannot be guaranteed by armaments and military alliances, but must rely on national understanding and the reduction of armaments. Therefore, the current Franco-Belgian military alliance must be abandoned. The defensive fortifications built by both sides and the implemented extension of military service law should be suspended immediately. He went on to say that the Association of Flemish War Veterans will launch a large-scale movement to oppose the Franco-Belgian military alliance and advocate that Belgium adopt a policy of voluntary neutrality. France has always regarded maintaining its superiority in the European army as its mission, and for a hundred years, it has always coveted the Rhineland, never diminishing. It is not a good way to ensure its own security for Belgium to conclude a military alliance with such a country, and if France can annex the Rhineland, then Belgium will inevitably be annexed by France. (20th National News Agency)

German Government Establishes Industrial Dumping Fund 65

(Berlin) Germany is about to establish a fund for industrial dumping. Recently, all industrial and commercial enterprises in the country with a business volume of more than 20,000 marks have received confidential letters from various economic institutions, informing them that they must abide by the order of Economics Minister Schacht and pay 2% to 15% of their total business volume to form the dumping fund. As for the amount to be paid by major enterprises, it will be designated by the authorities. For example, the Chemical Industry Association, whose business volume last year was 5,650,000,000 marks, must pay as much as 50,000,000 marks. The announcement issued by various economic institutions stated that paying the fund is indeed a huge sacrifice for industrial and commercial enterprises, but "for the sake of Germany's economic interests, the supply of raw materials is necessary, and sacrifices must be made with pain." (19th Havas Dispatch)

Roosevelt's Message to Congress, Re-Levy Heavy Taxes on the Wealthy to Equalize Wealth, Prevent Unrest Among American Society 66

(Washington) President Roosevelt today sent a special message to Congress, strongly advocating the levying of heavy taxes on the wealthy to equalize wealth and poverty. The President stated that he advocates a more widespread distribution of wealth in order to prevent unrest among American society, and stated that the United States must eventually simplify its corporate system through taxation. The first step should be to abolish useless holding companies in various industries. According to reports, the President's message greatly surprised most well-informed people. He also indicated that his opposition to holding companies is the starting point of a plan to equalize wealth and poverty. At the same time, he also strongly urged the amendment of the Constitution so that the federal government can issue securities to local governments in the future, and levy national taxes at the same time. Local governments can also levy local taxes on the securities issued by the federal government. The President also said that unrest in American society is becoming increasingly serious, so powerful methods must be used to reduce these dangers. People all know that the huge income of individuals is not only the result of talent and luck, but also greatly related to the opportunities given to them by the government. Therefore, it is only natural for the government to levy taxes to restrict them. Senator Long, who has always been the most enthusiastic supporter of wealth equalization plans, couldn't help but exclaim "Amen" when he heard the President's message today. Chairman Doughton of the House Ways and Means Committee said that the President requested that Congress be able to make a decision on his proposal during this session, so the Ways and Means Committee will consider it tomorrow. (19th National Telegram)

(Washington) President Roosevelt sent a special message to Congress today, advocating increasing taxes, especially paying attention to large incomes, large estates, and corporate net profits. This message came suddenly and was unexpected by outsiders. Personal income tax will definitely increase greatly, and corporate net profit tax will also increase progressively, from 10.75% to 16.75%, to replace the current 13.75%. In addition to the existing property tax, President Roosevelt also advocated levying estate tax and inheritance tax, and in order to prevent tax evasion, he also advocated levying gift tax. President Roosevelt claimed that he is in favor of substantially increasing personal income tax on large incomes and said that a corporate net profit tax of 13.75% regardless of the amount of profit is an inappropriate measure for small-scale businesses and should be adjusted according to economic capacity. President Roosevelt also proposed amending the Constitution so that the central government can levy income tax on the bonds issued by various states or local governments in the future, and the states and local governments can also levy taxes on the securities issued by the central government in the future. This message also requested that Congress continue to approve the various emergency donations recently voted on by the House of Representatives. (19th Reuters)

(Washington) Most Democrats and some Republicans strongly supported the method of amending income tax advocated by President Roosevelt in his special message submitted to Congress this morning. However, a few opponents said that implementing this proposal would further hinder recovery. Senator Long, who has always been difficult with President Roosevelt, claimed today that he does not trust President Roosevelt's promises, but if President Roosevelt can break up the financial groups, then the United States can escape the recession within 24 hours. (19th Reuters)

US Congress Passes Two Important Bills, Social Security Act and Labor Act 67

(Washington) The Social Security Act has been passed by both the Senate and the House of Representatives, and will take effect once President Roosevelt signs it. Afterwards, in addition to agricultural workers and domestic servants, 25 million American elderly and unemployed people can receive monthly subsidies, ranging from ten to eighty-five US dollars per person. When the Act begins to be implemented, the required funding will be almost entirely taken from taxes. Later, employers and employees will donate funds separately each year, and the amount will increase year by year, reaching its maximum limit in 1950, but at most it will not exceed 300 million US dollars. Starting this July, destitute men and women in the United States aged 65 or older or who are blind, if they meet the prescribed conditions, can receive a monthly living allowance of 15 US dollars from the government. Starting in 1937, employers and employees nationwide should donate 1% of the wages earned by workers and deposit it into the National Old-Age Insurance Fund. This percentage of donations will increase year by year, and in 1949, both employers and employees should each pay 3% of wages. By 1950, the total amount of donations may reach 200 million US dollars. Companies that already have pension systems that have been approved by the government are exempt from paying this donation. (20th Havas Dispatch)

(Washington) The House of Representatives recently passed the Labor Act proposed by Democratic Congressman Wagner, stipulating that labor-management disputes should be resolved through compulsory arbitration. Organizations with broad powers established by the management are prohibited from handling labor-management disputes. Protection measures are stipulated for workers who have not joined the union, and employers are prevented from interfering with labor groups. According to reports, this case was passed by the House of Representatives in December of last year. On the 17th of last month, the Senate made slight amendments and sent it back to the House of Representatives for review. It has now been passed by the House of Representatives again. (19th Havas Dispatch)

Director of the European and Asian Affairs Bureau of the Japanese Foreign Ministry, Togo Injured in Car Accident 68

(Tokyo) Togo Shigenori, Director of the European and Asian Affairs Bureau of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, was involved in a car accident when the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' car he was in drove past Kasumigaseki Road on the evening of the 19th. Japanese Troops Complete Rotation. 2,400 New Troops Arrive. 15 Trains of Japanese Soldiers Stop at Yuguan. 113

Tianjin Correspondence: The rotation of Japanese troops in Beiping and Tianjin. Due to the tension over the Hebei issue, the new troops arrived as scheduled, but the old troops' return was delayed. Now that the situation has eased, the Japanese troops along the Beiping-Tianjin and Beining lines are being rotated starting from the 18th. The first batch of returning troops, consisting of 700 artillery soldiers stationed in Tianjin, received a farewell speech from Commander Umezu at the Haiguang Temple barracks at 6:30 a.m. on the 18th and then boarded the Beining Railway car to Tanggu. At noon, they boarded the Honghayabusa Maru transport ship to return home. On the same day, the second batch left Tianjin at approximately 9:00 a.m., also boarding cars to Tanggu and boarding ships to return home. The Japanese troops stationed in Beiping are scheduled to pass through Tianjin at 10:00 a.m. on the 19th and go directly to Qinhuangdao, joining 1,600 Japanese soldiers from Tanggu, Tangshan, Changli, Leting, and Yuguan to board the Imperial ship Minghai Maru to return home. It is expected that the transfer of the old troops will be completed on the 21st. The newly arrived Japanese troops consist of three battalions, one artillery unit, and one cavalry unit, with additional communication squads, logistics teams, and gendarmerie, totaling more than 2,400 troops. Except for the officers, who have not been changed, they have been transported to Beiping and Tianjin from Tanggu and Qinhuangdao between the 12th and 14th of this month and distributed to garrison locations. Tianjin is garrisoning 920 infantry, artillery, and cavalry soldiers, Beiping is garrisoning 380 infantry, cavalry, and artillery soldiers, Tanggu is garrisoning 450 cavalry, infantry, artillery, and logistics soldiers, and Tangshan is garrisoning 320 cavalry, infantry, and artillery soldiers. Changli, Aoxian, Haiyangzhen, Gubeikou, and Saheqiao are each garrisoning a small squad of approximately 40 soldiers. The rest are garrisoned in Qinhuangdao and Shanhaiguan. The new troops are selected from the Second, Seventh, and Twelfth Divisions and are known as elite troops in the Japanese army. Now that the rotation of Japanese troops in the Beiping and Tianjin area has been completed, a large number of Japanese troops have suddenly arrived at Shanhaiguan and Gubeikou on the Great Wall line. In Gubeikou alone, there are 8-9,000 troops from the Sugihara Battalion's Kawagishi Brigade stationed in Chengde. The streets of Gubeikou and the vicinity of the Eastern Tombs are full of Japanese military tents, with flags everywhere. Japanese troops are also stationed in the territories of Huairou, Miyun, and Shunyi counties. From the 16th, field exercises have suddenly been held in the Shunyi-Yanqing area. The Kawagishi Brigade's headquarters is located in Gubeikou. It is claimed that the exercises will last for one month. Residents along the border are anxious and restless, and those fleeing inland are coming in an endless stream. Several thousand Japanese soldiers have also newly arrived from the customs area. The East Luocheng and inns in the city are all full. The Linyu County Government and Public Security Bureau have also been occupied, and the county government has moved to Haiyangzhen to conduct its affairs. Electric nets and sandbags have been piled up near the Japanese military camp in Nanda Camp, and the situation is particularly tense. Fifteen military trains are stopped at Yuguan Station, each train with 20-30 freight cars, all fully loaded with Japanese soldiers. As of the 16th, two trains left Shanhaiguan and headed to Suizhong Station on the pseudo-Fengshan Road, while the remaining thirteen trains still show no sign of leaving. More than 20 Japanese aircraft are parked at the Yuguan Airport, conducting low-altitude reconnaissance along the Beining Line every day. No one can know what the intention of such a display is. (18th)

Haiqi and Haichen: Failed Attempt to Escape. Land and Sea Battle on Night of Departure from Huangpu. Ran Aground Near Humen. Sailors Express Remorse. 114

Guangzhou Correspondence: The former Bohai Fleet, after defecting to Guangdong, was reorganized into the Guangdong Naval Fleet in April of the 22nd year of the Republic. In the spring of this year, the Guangdong authorities detected a conspiracy and, as a precaution, reorganized the fleet again in April, simultaneously replacing the captains of the Zhaohua, Haichen, and Haiqi. Chen Jitang concurrently served as the Naval Commander, and the original fleet commander Jiang Xiyuan was changed to principal of the naval academy. Although the senior officers on the three warships were replaced after the reorganization, the latent influence in the warships remained. They inevitably felt a sense of shared sorrow over the replacement of officers and had thoughts of returning north from time to time, but because the time was not yet ripe, and the army and key fortresses were heavily guarded, recently, the Naval Headquarters, to unify salaries, changed the salaries of the Haiqi and other three warships to small silver dollars. The sailors of the three warships became more resentful and secretly discussed escaping. One theory is that the warships and others plan to go north to join the pseudo-organization. The plan was decided, so they set fire to the ships at 11 pm on the 15th, and departed from the Huangpu River. The nearby land defense forces, including Chen Yuguang's Second Special Operations Battalion of the Salt Police Team, Xie Songnian's Marine Training Camp, and a battalion of the Marine Special Operations Battalion, had been on guard against the three warships in advance. As soon as the Haiqi and others left, they were discovered by the sentries of the Salt Police Special Operations Battalion and reported to their superiors for instructions, while firing guns to stop them. The officers and soldiers on the warships also returned fire, and the sound of gunfire and cannons resounded for a time. The villagers near Huangpu, unaware of the inside story, moved away one after another. The Haiqi and Haichen fired cannons along the way in retaliation, causing the Second Battalion of the Salt Police on land to suffer one platoon leader and more than ten soldiers wounded. After the news reached the provincial capital, Chen Jitang telegraphed the coastal defense forces to strictly stop them and ordered the Humen Fortress Commander to open fire on the Haiqi and other ships to intercept them. That night, the Haichen and Haiqi also fired large cannons to counter the Humen Fortress, and traffic on the Humen sea was cut off for a time. On the morning of the 16th, the Guangzhou-Hong Kong ships entering the inner river from Hong Kong could not pass and returned to Hong Kong one after another. Passengers then changed to the Guangzhou-Kowloon railway to return to the province. The Haichen and Haiqi warships (the Zhaohua did not join because of machine damage) ran aground and could not proceed as they approached Humen. The Humen fortresses used new type artillery for shooting, and more than a dozen aircraft were dispatched from Guangzhou to pursue and bombard them at night, and the firepower was very fierce. The Haiqi and Haichen were forced to drop anchor in the sea near Lotus Mountain and wait for mediation. At about 9 p.m. on the 16th, Chen Vice Commander, Wu Deputy, and Wang Captain, as representatives, landed from the Yuzhu Fortress to contact the province. At the same time, the officers and soldiers of the Haiqi and Haichen warships also sent two telegrams to the Navy Department as follows: (1) "To Acting Commander Chen and Deputy Commander Zhang (Zhiying), we are preparing to sail for reasons of livelihood and to seek a new path. Heaven is above, and we have no choice but to do this. The soldiers have been under your command for two years, and you should know our hearts, and we have not touched anything about the Guangdong government. We are now fully remorseful and willing to return the fleet to you. We respectfully ask you to send representatives to the warships for contact, or representatives from the Haiqi and Haichen warships can come to the department. The entire staff and soldiers of Haiqi and Haichen bow down." (2) "(Title Omitted) The Haiqi and Haichen have dropped anchor, and the soldiers have realized their remorse. Please indicate how to contact us to ensure the safety of the sailors on the two warships and of Hao (Captain Chen Hao of the Haichen warship). We are grateful, otherwise people and boats will perish together, which would be shameful to the Chinese people. The entire staff and soldiers of Haiqi and Haichen and Chen Hao bow down." After receiving the telegram, Chen Jitang agreed to meet with the representatives of the two warships to discuss the aftermath. At the same time, Chen made a statement saying that Zhaohua's lack of blind adherence and continued berthing at Huangpu was deeply appreciated. The soldiers of the Haichen and Haiqi warships were threatened and committed treason, but now they are remorseful and not entirely unforgivable, and it is not impossible to give them a way to reform themselves. The two warships are old and have no combat power, and their retention has little to do with Guangdong's coastal defense, and their existence is only a waste of public funds. If they are truly remorseful, it may be possible to ask the Southwest Political Affairs Council to consider lenient treatment, etc. On the 17th, the two sides were still in contact, and Humen had not been relieved. (June 17)

Hankou's Commercial Decline. Losses Account for More Than 60%. Trade Associations Offer Six Relief Suggestions. 115

Hankou Correspondence: Hubei Province has suffered frequent disasters, rural areas are declining, and urban commerce is greatly affected, and is trending towards collapse. Hankou is also destined to suffer the same fate. Now that the year 23 of the Republic is coming to an end, the settlements in various industries are showing a significant fact of commercial collapse. This is truly a serious social problem that cannot be taken lightly. According to the investigation, there are about 133 industries in Hankou, all with trade associations. There are a total of 8,109 shops that have joined trade associations, and 1,695 shops that have not joined trade associations. After analyzing and statistically analyzing the settlement situation of shops that have joined trade associations, only 685 shops have made a profit, accounting for 9% of the total, 2,396 shops can barely maintain, accounting for 29% of the total, 4,035 shops have suffered losses, accounting for 50% of the total, and 989 shops have closed down, accounting for 12% of the total. The decline can be seen. As for the reasons for the decline, there are several points: (1) rural bankruptcy and weak purchasing power, (2) inability to recover credit sales and many collapses, (3) too many businesses in the same industry do not join the trade association, competing to reduce prices, and everyone is affected, (4) too high donations, taxes and freight, (5) unable to resist foreign goods dumping. The trade association plans to offer six relief methods: (1) request the government to do its best to protect the interests of creditors, cooperation with the trade association, and find ways to recover debts from debtors, (2) ask the government to reduce taxes, donations and freight, and the trade association will save expenses on its own, (3) contact the trade association, rectify trade rules, standardize market prices, and crack down on businesses in the same industry that have not joined the trade association, (4) contact cooperatives to implement production and credit cooperation, (5) request the government to allocate funds for relief, or the commercial bank will provide credit loans with low interest, (6) advise businesses in the same industry to improve their business and improve the quality of goods. However, it is still uncertain whether it will be able to overcome this economic panic. (19th)

Anhui Provincial Government Orders Counties to Provide Emergency Relief for Drought - Eight Measures Proposed - 116

Anqing Correspondence: Since the beginning of summer, Anhui Province has experienced scarce rainfall, leading to drought conditions in various areas. People generally fear a recurrence of last year's drought. Fortunately, substantial rainfall occurred on the 14th and 15th, easing public anxiety. However, the provincial government recognizes that after successive disasters, rural areas are impoverished, and widespread displacement makes them vulnerable to famine. It previously directed the Finance Department to negotiate with the China Industrial Bank for an overdraft loan of 100,000 yuan, specifically for seed loans to the counties. This loan has now been processed, totaling 71,000 yuan. To prevent future interest charges, the government has formulated emergency drought relief measures and instructed the counties to implement them. The measures are as follows: (1) Opening dikes to divert water: Where there are no sluice gates for diversion, the dike-opening and water-diversion methods promulgated last year can be applied. When necessary, the water conservancy personnel in charge should assess the terrain and handle matters appropriately, also overseeing the dredging of ditches and canals within the dikes so that the diverted water can provide widespread irrigation. (Attached: Dike-Opening Methods) (2) Adding Equipment: Since last year, counties have been repeatedly ordered to purchase water pumps. If financial resources are insufficient, local artisans should be supervised to build dragon-bone waterwheels for use. (3) Utilizing Water Sources: Since last October, counties have been repeatedly ordered to build more waterways, ponds, and weirs, and to open up new water sources. The current need is for practical on-site investigations of water sources, guiding irrigation. (4) Aiding with Wells: Last year, counties were ordered to use well-digging as a means of drought prevention. Where water sources are insufficient, prompt supervision of the digging of ten wells is needed, with the full exploration of nearby areas rich in springs, to stimulate groundwater volume and ensure widespread irrigation. (Attached: Simplified Spring Exploration Methods) (5) Cooperative Irrigation: In applying the above methods, the following should still be noted: People often differ in their interests, lacking unity, and watch their crops wither, failing to take action. The problem lies not in the absence of water sources, but in the lack of farmer organization. Each district should be supervised to ensure that wherever there is a water source, efforts should be made to open waterways and divert irrigation, without fearing indirect routes. The manpower and tools required for water diversion and waterway opening can be collected and applied based on the benefiting acreage. If water pumps are needed, funds should be raised to purchase or rent them. Furthermore, during severe droughts, disputes over water for irrigation easily arise, so preventive maintenance should be a priority to avoid hindering cooperation. (6) Early Crop Switching: In particularly high and dry areas where irrigation is deemed difficult, prompt switching to drought-resistant crops should be ordered. (7) Diligent Weed Removal: Weeds consume the most water and compete with crops for growth, so they should be urgently removed. (8) Loosening Surface Soil: Loosening surface soil can disrupt the existing capillary structure of the soil, preventing moisture from rising, reducing evaporation, and maintaining the soil's inherent moisture. Furthermore, diligent weeding can also remove weeds, and the removed weeds can be used to cover the roots of crops to block direct sunlight. (June 17th)

Fengxian: Using Baojia System to Eliminate Locusts 120

In Ping'an, Sankan, and Liangxiang townships in the county's Fifth District, locust nymphs have recently proliferated in the area outside the dikes within the reed marshes, spreading rapidly over an area of four to five li. County Magistrate and Director of Agricultural Extension Chu Shangda have established a locust extermination office there to provide on-site guidance for elimination, and are purchasing locusts at a price of 160 cash per catty. It is said that over 300 yuan has already been spent. District Chief Xia seized the opportunity to utilize the Baojia system, recently summoning the Baojia chiefs of various townships to the office to discuss the matter. It was decided that each household would send one worker to jointly exterminate the locusts using ditch-digging and fire-burning methods. Most of the firewood is provided by the villagers, and the remainder is purchased with funds from the locust extermination office. Since the implementation of this method, it has been very effective, the locust infestation is gradually being eliminated, and the spread can be avoided.

Suzhou: Modern Woman Commits Suicide in Hotel 121

On the evening of the 19th, a modern woman, claiming to be Chen Jin-sao, 18 years old, from outside Qimen, with beautiful features, arrived at the Da Dong Hotel outside the 　Gate. She initially booked room 250, but then, disliking its exposed location, changed to room 249. She asked the tea boy if Qian Su-zhen had arrived, and if any men from Shanghai had come to visit, among other questions. She then ordered two pieces of pine nut candy from the tea boy. At 2:00 AM on the 20th, Xi Xiaohua, a guest in the room opposite 249, noticed unusual noises from within the room. He urgently reported this to the front desk, who forced the door open. Chen had already taken poison and was unconscious. Opium stains were scattered inside the tea cup. A photo with a man's hand on it, was found on the table, but it had been cut up. After being taken to Suyong Hospital, she died because the poison had gone too deep. It appeared that the case was due to a broken heart. Since no relatives could be found, the court ordered the local authorities to prepare a coffin and burial after investigation.

Local News

Ministry of Finance's Taxation Department Convenes Meeting of Tobacco, Alcohol, and Stamp Tax Bureau Chiefs - Chiefs and Deputy Chiefs of Ten Provincial Tax Bureaus Attend Revenue Consolidation Meeting - Session Scheduled for Five Days 126

Central News Agency: In order to consolidate national tobacco, alcohol, and stamp tax revenues, the Taxation Department of the Ministry of Finance convened a meeting of the tobacco, alcohol, and stamp tax bureau chiefs of various provinces in Shanghai. The opening ceremony was held at 9 AM yesterday morning in the Junpu Bureau conference room on the fifth floor of the Jianghai Customs House. The session is scheduled for five days, with the closing ceremony to be held on the morning of the 24th. Minister of Finance Kong will also attend to give instructions. Details are recorded below:

Attending Bureau Chiefs

The opening ceremony of the meeting of the tobacco, alcohol, and stamp tax bureau chiefs of various provinces was held at 9 AM yesterday morning. The bureau chiefs from various provinces who attended included: Anhui (Chief) Jing Xuxin, Fujian (Chief) Wang Guanghui, Jiangxi (Chief) Jing Youyan, Henan (Chief) Liang Dacheng, Hubei (Deputy) Yang Duo, Shandong (Deputy) Fu Zhengshun, Zhejiang (Chief) Zhao Jinqing (Deputy) Huang Zupei, Jiangsu (Chief) Sheng Shengyi (Deputy) Xue Futian, Hunan (Chief) Tang Yan, Hebei (Chief) Ding Chungao, and others. The Taxation Department attendees included: Director Wu Qiding, Secretaries Dong Zhongding, Zhou Jiechun, Section Chiefs Fang Yunxian, Jiang Yongyi, Hong Yi, Chen Jun, Inspector Tang Shi, and others, for a total of 29 people.

Wu's Address

The meeting was presided over by Director Wu Qiding, who led the attendees in performing the usual formalities before giving his opening address. He said that the tobacco and alcohol taxes had been in place for a long time, with deep-rooted malpractices. In recent years, he had made great efforts to consolidate them, and tax revenues had increased year by year in the 21st and 22nd years, with gradual progress. He hoped to eliminate the dross and impurity, and make steady progress. However, in the 23rd year, the various bureaus reported that tax revenues as of March of this year, those that had met their quotas accounted for only one or two tenths. The rest fell short of the amount, with some only reaching thirty to forty percent. The huge shortfall was unprecedented. Tax systems are not easy to be made full, it must be a case of lax or strained implementation. The reason for this must be examined in detail and remedies sought urgently. Otherwise, the situation will become increasingly dire and irreversible. This is the fundamental purpose of convening this meeting. There are two ways to consolidate: one is to continue as before, and the other is to make a fresh start. The key is to adapt to the situation and proceed gradually in an orderly manner. The public sales fees and taxes in provinces such as Hebei and Shandong, and the fixed-amount taxes and special taxes in provinces such as Jiangsu and Zhejiang, the collection of receipts, the verification of transport documents, the tax amounts have to be compared with the amounts, and the submission of reports have fixed procedures, the legislation has never been made in secret, and the system has never been stringent, just that it has been accumulated over a long period of time, the power to tax has been abused, the tax thieves and cunning subordinates collude with each other, the statutes and regulations are regarded as insignificant, the rules and regulations are ignored, the malpractices are numerous, and cannot be investigated. Is this not a defect in the tax system, or a failure to implement it effectively? How should we reaffirm the existing regulations, strictly prohibit violations, and enforce the law without fault, establishing a fence? This is one aspect of adhering to the old regulations and strictly following them. Taxation should be based on the principles of simplicity and fairness. The current taxes on domestic tobacco and alcohol, whether inherited from old regulations or implemented under new systems, vary from place to place. This was originally a temporary measure. The types of taxes are becoming increasingly complex, and production and sales are changing frequently. What was suitable in the past may not be suitable today, and what is beneficial here may not be suitable there. A fundamental consolidation is urgently needed. However, a complete reform may not be possible in a hurry, and a sudden change may create obstacles. How should we select key issues to address and set an example? This is another aspect of planning for innovation and adopting a gradual approach. Which should be retained and which should be reformed? I hope everyone will express their views and create a plan that is neither conservative nor radical, and that is both feasible and workable. Once the standards are in place, the direction can be followed, and the future of the tobacco administration will be promising. Furthermore, laws cannot be implemented on their own. It is also important to have people to administer them. If we compare and weigh the successes and failures of the tobacco administration over the years, the changes in the system, and the amounts of revenue collected, we can deeply reflect on the reasons for the rise and fall. Gentlemen, you have experience both domestically and internationally, and have deep knowledge and expertise. After the meeting is over, bring the resolutions back with you, lead your staff, encourage each other, and put them into practice. Those who have already surpassed their quotas should not be complacent, but should strive for further progress. Those who have not met their quotas should be strictly supervised and urged to increase their revenue. By working together and overcoming the difficulties of the time, this meeting will not be in vain.

Conference Proposals

The conference has 32 proposals, which are classified according to their nature as follows: (A) Branch Bureau Collection System and Organization: (1) Proposal to truly determine the quota and strictly implement performance evaluation (Taxation Department Proposal 1); (2) Proposal to implement a contract system for tobacco and alcohol taxes in order to ensure that the tax amount is fixed (Fujian Bureau Proposal); (3) Proposal to request consideration of the selection committee method, fixing the quota and limiting collection and remittance to increase tax revenue (Hubei Bureau Proposal); (4) Proposal to allocate the tobacco and alcohol tax quota in Shandong Province according to peak and off-peak months (Shandong Bureau Proposal); (5) Proposal to establish bureaus by district to facilitate consolidation (Hunan Bureau Proposal); (6) Proposal to return the local tobacco tax of Deng County and Xichuan County to this bureau for collection from the 24th year onward in order to clarify authority and facilitate consolidation (Henan Bureau Proposal); (7) Proposal to request that the Taxation Department instruct officials to prepare and submit tables of quotas and actual remittance amounts for each branch bureau in advance (Taxation Department Proposal 2); (B) Tax Collection Methods and Permits: (1) Proposal on which types of alcohol can be changed to a one-time collection (Taxation Department Proposal 4); (2) Proposal to merge the names of tobacco and alcohol taxes in Shandong Province for collection (Shandong Bureau Proposal); (3) Proposal to unify tobacco and alcohol prices to maintain commerce and increase tax revenue (Shandong Bureau Proposal); (4) Proposal to formulate methods for consolidating the collection of tobacco and alcohol taxes to increase tax revenue (Hunan Bureau Proposal); (5) Proposal to conduct tobacco and alcohol business registration in Anhui Province (Anhui Bureau Proposal); (6) Proposal to separately tax tobacco leaves made into tobacco shreds for non-cigarette use (Taxation Department Proposal 5); (7) Proposal to change the special tax on tobacco leaves to a tax on tobacco shreds (Fujian Bureau Proposal); (8) Proposal to revise the tax rate on local tobacco leaves in Anhui Province (Anhui Bureau Proposal); (9) Proposal to implement fixed-amount tax permits and zero-catty tax certificates for special local tobacco leaves in the coming year (Taxation Department Proposal 6); (10) Proposal to change the tax certificate for local tobacco to a fixed-amount tax certificate to facilitate auditing (Jiangxi Bureau Proposal); (11) Proposal to revise the form of the tax certificate (Jiangsu Bureau Proposal); (12) A brief statement of the situation of shortfalls in alcohol tax, proposing to change to a unified tax or implement a monopoly system (Requested by the Shanghai Shaoxing Alcohol Association); C. Branch Bureau Expenses and Rewards: (1) Proposal to increase the expenses of each branch bureau for tobacco and alcohol taxes (Proposed by Jiangsu Bureau); (2) Proposal to use a progressive bonus system in addition to the 16% commission for each branch bureau's over-collection of tobacco and alcohol taxes to show encouragement (Fujian Bureau Proposal); (3) Proposal to request that the department formulate a full-year collection bonus method for tobacco and alcohol tax branch bureau chiefs and local tobacco special tax branch bureau chiefs to encourage them (Henan Bureau Proposal); (4) Proposal to increase the expenses of each district's tobacco and alcohol branch bureau and issue permits based on actual needs to facilitate implementation (Hebei Bureau Proposal); (D) Anti-Smuggling and Inspection: (1) Proposal to establish special inspections to strictly enforce the affixing of liquor tax certificates and local tobacco stamps, etc., to prevent each branch bureau from transferring them to each other, attached with methods to assist in the inspection of stamps (Taxation Department Proposal 2); (2) Seriously investigate pending cases (Taxation Department Proposal 3); (3) Request that each province assist in anti-smuggling (Jiangsu Bureau Proposal); (4) Proposal to request that the department consult with the provincial governments to include the responsibility of county magistrates to assist tax authorities in the county magistrate's performance evaluation (Henan Bureau Proposal); (5) Proposal to organize and train tax police to eliminate long-standing malpractices and facilitate collection (Hubei Bureau Proposal); (E) Revision of Penalties: (1) Request to revise the penalties for the fixed-amount tax on local alcohol (Jiangsu Bureau Proposal); (2) Change the rules for fine-based awards to benefit tax revenue (Shandong Bureau Proposal); (F) Improvement of Planting and Brewing: (1) Proposal to request that the department appoint agricultural technology experts to go to the tobacco-producing areas to seek all possible improvements (Hubei Bureau Proposal); (2) Proposal for government and merchants to jointly establish an organization to provide loans to rural areas to improve tobacco seeds and provide loans to brewing and tobacco merchants to subsidize the purchase of brewing materials and tobacco leaves to benefit production (Zhejiang Bureau Proposal).

Subgroup Review

The general meeting did not discuss the proposals yesterday morning. However, after the chairman announced the catalog of proposals, it was decided to divide the proposals into two groups for review. The first group will review 23 proposals, including (A) Branch Bureau Collection System and Organization, (B) Tax Collection Methods and Permits, and (C) Branch Bureau Expenses and Rewards. The second group will review 9 proposals, including (D) Anti-Smuggling and Inspection, (E) Revision of Penalties, and (F) Improvement of Planting and Brewing. After consolidating and reviewing the proposals based on the Taxation Department's proposals, they will be submitted to the general meeting for discussion.

Meeting Schedule

The meeting is scheduled for five days. After the opening ceremony yesterday morning, subgroup meetings will be held in the afternoon today (21st) to review the proposals. A general meeting will be held tomorrow (22nd) morning to discuss the proposals. Sunday, the 23rd, will be a recess. The closing ceremony will be held on the morning of the 24th. Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi will attend the meeting and deliver a speech.

Copious Rainfall in this City Last Night and This Morning - Abrupt Drop in Temperature in this City to Only 70 Degrees - Slight Drop in Grain Market Prices and Stable Transactions 127

Since the rainfall of 0.63 inches in this city on the 16th, people's hearts have been largely settled, and the anxiety in the market has also been slightly reduced. From 2:30 PM the day before yesterday until this morning, there was heavy rain again, totaling 30.5 mm. After the farmland received this irrigation, people were even more gratified. Details are recorded as follows:

Heavy Rain the Day Before Yesterday: From 2:30 PM the day before yesterday, the southeast wind in this city gradually tightened, followed by continuous rain. After 5 PM, the raindrops gradually increased, and after 8 PM, there was even heavier torrential rain. The wind also shifted from southeast to northeast, and the rain continued until 9 AM this morning, totaling 30.5 mm, or 1.2 inches. According to the Astronomical Observatory, if the wind direction shifts to the northwest, the sky will clear. The temperature this morning was lower than the previous day, with a minimum of 68 degrees and 70.5 degrees at 11 AM. The highest temperature the previous day was 84.2 degrees.

Farmland Rejuvenation: According to reports from various places, since the drought in Jiangnan and the north, more than half of the farmland has withered, cotton seedlings are difficult to sprout, rice seedlings are difficult to transplant, the soil is scorched, and the river water has dried up. Since the rainfall on the 16th, and the timely heavy rain the day before yesterday, the fields along the Jinghu, Huhangyong, and other areas, and the coastal ports in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, can all be rejuvenated. The farmers who rely on rain have been praying and making offerings for rain. This concept has been completely dispelled.

Transactions Trending Towards Stability: Before the rain, people in the rice and wheat markets were anxious and apprehensive. Speculators took advantage of the situation, causing considerable disruption to the market. After two heavy rains in a row this week, market transactions have stabilized. Yesterday, flour had already dropped by 0.03 to 0.05 yuan compared to the previous day, and three markets had already opened by 10:30 AM. The price of rice fell by 0.2 yuan, and the wheat market was also very stable. It is generally regarded as weak in the market, but in reality, it is stable.

Municipal Public Bonds: Yesterday Morning's Lottery Redemption; 261 Winning Tickets Drawn, Totaling $280,000; Payments to Be Made by the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications Starting June 30th 128

The $3.5 million Shanghai Municipal Public Bonds issued by our municipal government on the 23rd year [of the Republic] held their first lottery redemption at the Bankers' Association yesterday morning at 9:00 AM. A total of 34 winning tickets with a face value of $5,000, 97 winning tickets with a face value of $1,000, and 130 winning tickets with a face value of $100 were drawn. Details are as follows:

Attending Representatives

Including Cai Zengji, Director of the Municipal Finance Bureau; Lin Jinzi of the Auditing Department; Pu Ming of the Ministry of Finance; Lu Shuping of the Municipal Government; Xu Jiluan of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Liu Wuqiao of the Money Guild; Jin Wenyuan of the Central Bank of China; Cao Zhenming of the Bank of China; Mao Duan of the Bank of Communications; Wu Zhide of the Shanghai Municipal Bank; and over 20 staff members from the Finance Bureau.

Chairman's Report

Chairman Cai Zengji began by reporting, stating briefly: "The total amount of the Shanghai Municipal Public Bonds issued in the 23rd year of the Republic was $3.5 million, issued last July and underwritten by the [Syndicate] Bank, organized by [New] Foreign Bank. The revenue from the city's special automobile license fees is allocated to the bond fund, which is entrusted to the National Debt Fund Management Committee for safekeeping. It is stipulated that, starting from June of the 24th year of the Republic, the bonds will be redeemed by lottery over 12 years, with a lottery redemption held once every June. Today marks the first lottery redemption, with a total principal to be redeemed of $280,000. All winning bonds and matured interest coupons will be paid by the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications starting from June 30th of this year. I ask that everyone verify the winning numbers for execution of the lottery."

Lottery Instructions

1. The public bonds are divided into three types: $5,000, $1,000, and $100. There are 427 $5,000 tickets, totaling $2.135 million; 1,207 $1,000 tickets, totaling $1.207 million; and 1,580 $100 tickets, totaling $158,000. The total amount is $3.5 million.

2. This redemption is for $280,000, accounting for 8% of the total. However, because the numbers of each type of bond start from number one, ordinary methods cannot be used for the lottery.

3. Based on the number of bonds issued, the average is calculated at 8%. There are 427 $5,000 bonds, so 34 tickets should win, totaling $170,000. The total amount of winning bond tickets is $280,000.

4. The winning numbers are drawn sequentially from the total numbers of each bond. For example, 427 $5,000 bonds were issued, so numbers from 1 to 427, a total of 427, are placed in the lottery drum. 34 numbers are drawn sequentially, and the numbers drawn are the winning numbers for the $5,000 bonds. The winning numbers for the $1,000 and $100 bonds are drawn in the same manner.

Winning Numbers

The New Jiangtian Steamer; Cabin Steward Dispute Resolved; The Ship Is Expected to Resume Sailing Tomorrow 134

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Shanghai-Ningbo passenger ship New Jiangtian announced the suspension of its service to the reorganization of cabin staff, the removal of the "cold water gang". The cabin staff have now indicated compliance and registered as ordered, so the company plans to resume sailing tomorrow. The details are as follows:

Abolition of the "Cold Water Gang"

In addition to the regular cabin stewards on the New Jiangtian, there was also the so-called "cold water gang" of assistant cabin stewards, whose numbers were twice that of the regular cabin stewards. As a result, passengers boarding the ship would see nothing but cabin stewards, while the regular cabin stewards could do nothing and pocket huge profits. The company's first point in reforming the cabin staff system was to limit the number of cabin stewards and clerks and order the informal "cold water gang" cabin stewards to leave the ship immediately and not be allowed to board the New Jiangtian again. This has now been done.

Cabin Stewards Agreed to Register

The suspension of the ship was caused by the cabin stewards' resistance to registration. Since the suspension on Monday, the cabin stewards on board have also realized that opposition will not solve the problem. Therefore, since yesterday, the regular cabin stewards have gradually complied and no longer resolutely resist. When the company sent staff to the ship to order everyone to register, the cabin stewards expressed acceptance and automatically filled out and submitted the registration forms issued by the company, attaching their photos for verification.

Agreed Number of Cabin Stewards

According to regulations, the number of cabin stewards on the New Jiangtian should only be over 170, but there are currently over 280 people. In order to temporarily maintain everyone's livelihood, the company still registers and hires over 280 people, but does not allow the hiring of assistants. This point has also been agreed upon. However, it is rumored that if so many cabin stewards are not needed on the ship, the company may select a portion of them to stay in Shanghai for training, in preparation for assigning them to other ships in the future. This matter is still under negotiation.

Eliminate Bad Habits

The cabin stewards on the ship do not have salaries and rely entirely on passengers' tips and alcohol commissions for the majority of their income. However, the company has not collected deposits or guarantee money from these cabin stewards. Therefore, the company is now discussing new regulations to eliminate the bad habit of demanding alcohol commissions from passengers. The cabin stewards will be paid wages by the company, provisionally set at $16 per month per person, plus a food allowance of $5. Since the cabin stewards have wages and food, they are not allowed to demand a single cent from passengers. The company will issue a notice and print it on the ship tickets, advising passengers not to give tips privately, to avoid undermining the new system. The company will spend over $5,000 per month in this way.

Resuming Service on Saturday

Since all issues have been resolved, the new system can be easily implemented. Yesterday, General Manager Liu Hongsheng discussed with the heads of various departments and decided that the suspension of the New Jiangtian was due to the elimination of the "cold water gang" and the reformation of the cabin stewards. Now that the cabin stewards have expressed obedience, there is no need to continue the suspension. It was decided to resume normal service starting on Saturday (the 21st), and the incident can be considered over.

Representatives of Overseas Chinese Aiding in Siam; Returned to Shanghai Yesterday from Nanjing; Refuting the Talks of the Siamese Delegation 135

The United Association of Shanghai groups assisting overseas Chinese in Siam, previously sent five representatives - Huang Jianzhong of the Overseas Chinese United Association, Chen Luqin of the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association, Zheng Jikai of the Guangdong Fellow Villagers Association, Zhang Nanyin of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and Guo Qiming of the Chaozhou Fellow Villagers Association - to Nanjing on the 15th to request the central government to sign a commercial treaty with Siam as soon as possible, and to negotiate the issue of Siam's unreasonable oppression of our overseas Chinese. The results were quite satisfactory. The petition delegation has now completed its mission. Except for Zheng Jikai, Zhang Nanyin, and Guo Qiming, who returned to Shanghai on the 19th, Chen Luqin and Huang Jianzhong also returned to Shanghai yesterday one after another. It is learned that the association is scheduled to convene an executive committee meeting tomorrow (the 22nd) to report the results of the petition in Nanjing and to discuss sending personnel to Fujian, Guangdong, Hong Kong and other places to negotiate the implementation of the embargo on Siamese rice. A reporter from Shen Shi News Agency asked Chen Luqin, secretary of the Overseas Chinese United Association, at the association's office on [Avenue] Dubail yesterday about the Siamese Far East delegation's denial of the Siamese government's anti-Chinese activities. Chen replied as follows:

Satisfactory Results of the Petition in Nanjing

Chen first reported on the details of the petition in Nanjing, stating briefly: "The five representatives of the petition delegation took the 11:00 PM express train to Nanjing on the 15th, and arrived in the capital at 7:00 AM the next morning. They immediately met with the welcoming representatives from Nanjing to discuss the petition and the joint delivery of a memorandum to the Siamese delegation. Later, due to fatigue from the journey, they opened room 363 at the Central Hotel to rest briefly and planned the steps to be taken for the petition on the 17th. On the morning of the 17th, they submitted petitions to the Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission. Secretary-General Ye Chuqing of the Central Party Headquarters received them and expressed his appreciation for the delegation's enthusiasm in assisting overseas Chinese, and promised to forward the petition to the central government immediately, ordering Ambassador Jiang in Japan to continue negotiations with Siam. They also joined the Joint Association of Nanjing Municipal Agricultural, Industrial, Commercial, Academic, and Women's Groups to deliver a memorandum to the Siamese delegation at the Overseas Chinese Reception Center, asking them to convey to the Siamese government the Chinese people's hope that the Siamese government would abolish various harsh regulations that abuse overseas Chinese and improve the treatment of overseas Chinese. In the afternoon, they hosted the Nanjing news media at the Central Hotel, with dozens of reporters from various newspapers attending. Huang Jianzhong reported on the purpose and mission of the petition and the situation of Siamese oppression of overseas Chinese. Representatives of various newspapers also spoke one after another, expressing their willingness to fulfill their journalistic duty. The atmosphere at the venue was quite tense. In the evening, Xiao Jishan, a standing committee member of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, also hosted a banquet to welcome the representatives. The representatives called, ran around, and suffered much in Nanjing for several days, but fortunately the results were quite satisfactory and somewhat comforting."

Denying Anti-Chinese Activities is Evading Responsibility and Covering Up

Chen then replied to the reporter's question about the Siamese delegation's denial of anti-Chinese activities. Chen expressed regret that most of the points mentioned by the delegation ignored the existing facts. "We have received reports from overseas Chinese groups in Siam, which can be used as evidence. The reports state briefly that Tuayue, a resident of Thonburi and Bukhalo districts near Bangkok, is the leader of the Siamese Tram Workers' Union. He had previously been ordered by the leader of the Siamese People's Party to incite Chinese rice mill workers to demand wage increases, which led to a major strike. Tuayue took advantage of the labor-management disputes of the overseas Chinese to nationalize the Chinese factories, allowing Siamese workers to enjoy the benefits. Now, on May 23, on the grounds of facilitating business and providing relief to Siamese workers, he submitted a petition to the Siamese Labor Bureau, requesting the Labor Bureau to establish rice mills and lumber mills. After receiving the petition, the Labor Bureau considered the matters presented to be outside the scope of the Labor Bureau and forwarded the petition to the government for review, which is expected to be approved. As mentioned above, Siam's anti-Chinese actions continue to arise. The various points mentioned by the delegation are excuses and cover-ups, which cannot be denied."

Changing the Compulsory Courses is Just Perfunctory

Regarding the suppression of overseas Chinese education, Chen said, "The Siamese Ministry of Education previously proposed a compromise of compulsory classes because our people rose up in opposition, and the various harsh regulations imposed on overseas Chinese aroused public indignation, and even advocated boycotting Siamese rice as a punishment. In order to ease the people's anger, they had proposed to allow Chinese schools to re-register, and petition the Siamese government to establish compulsory classes within the schools. However, news came from Siam that none of the Chinese schools that went to the Ministry of Education to register were approved, because the Siamese government is still taking a wait-and-see attitude towards our people. As for the Siamese Far East delegation's statement that Siam has not forced foreign-run schools to teach Siamese, only required a few hours of Siamese language per week, it is clear that they are trying to cover up and deceive the Chinese people. Last year, the Siamese Ministry of Education issued a notice to all Chinese schools to establish compulsory classes, and the curriculum required 23 hours of Siamese language per week. The regulations of the Ministry of Education have been translated and published in newspapers, and the Chinese people have long known about them. The regulations also force overseas Chinese children between the ages of seven and fourteen to receive compulsory education in Siamese schools. The facts are clear, and there is no point in covering them up."

Sending Personnel to Hong Kong and Guangdong to Boycott Siamese Rice

Chen finally said, "The five representatives plan to convene on the 21st for a consultation, and tomorrow they will hold a standing committee meeting to implement the dispatch of personnel to Guangzhou, Hong Kong, Xiamen and other places to coordinate the implementation of the boycott of Siamese rice imports, in order to promote the awakening of the Siamese government. Before the two countries sign a treaty, we must first achieve the following three expectations: (1) In politics, abolish the military service of overseas Chinese in Siam. (2) In economics, abolish various harsh taxes and levies. (3) In education, abolish the order to force Chinese soldiers to read selected texts for 23 hours. Whether Chinese children should read Siamese language should be ordered by our Ministry of Education itself, and Chinese school teachers should not be forced to take Siamese language exams by the Siamese government. If the above three items can be achieved, then the feelings of the people of the two countries can naturally become more friendly, and the mutual signing of a commercial treaty between the two countries can also reach its goal sooner."

The Shanghai Municipal Council Considers; The Use of the Old Central Police Station Building 140

According to the Shanghai Times, the Shanghai Municipal Council has recently moved the Central Police Station to a new building on Fuzhou Road. Due to the poor market conditions and financial emergency in Shanghai, the original plan to rebuild the old building has been postponed indefinitely. However, it will not be left vacant for long. The Municipal Council has considered temporarily repairing it to house some police officers. When the market turns around, a new building will be rebuilt. Several suggestions have been submitted to the Municipal Council, but none have been definitively decided. One proposal was to build a municipal hall on the site of the old Central Police Station and the current Central Fire Department, with the Municipal Council's library attached. This proposal was well-received by the Municipal Council, but the cost is huge, and the Municipal Council's current financial resources cannot afford it. According to a member of the Municipal Council yesterday, there is hope of implementing it when financial resources are slightly more available in the future. The most urgent matter now is to move the Central Fire Department to a more suitable location. The Municipal Council has acknowledged that the current building is not only unsuitable for use, but also very dangerous, as the huge fire engines frequently enter and exit, and the vibrations have made the building shake greatly. The new extension of the [Wayside Jail] West Jail on Ward Road is about to be completed, and the foreign prisoners held in the West Jail on Xiamen Road will all be moved in. Therefore, the building on Xiamen Road will be demolished and a new building will be built to house the Central Fire Department. However, the new building will require several months to complete.

Ning's Creditors Held a Meeting Yesterday 142

Due to financial difficulties, the Ningbo Industrial Bank announced a suspension of payments. Subsequently, its founder, Wu Zhihao, went into hiding, and there has been no news of resumption of business or liquidation. Creditors, led by Zhang Zilian, formed a creditors' association and began registration. Yesterday, they convened a meeting of creditors in the assembly hall of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, electing fifteen representatives to appeal to various parties, demanding the bank's repayment. The details of the meeting are recorded below:

Attendance of Creditors: The creditors' meeting of Ningbo Industrial Bank was held yesterday afternoon from 2:00 PM in the assembly hall of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Over 270 creditors attended, mostly small merchants and artisans from Ningbo, with a considerable number of fashionable young men and women. The atmosphere at the meeting was very tense, with a strong hope for repayment. When the chairman reported, "Demanding the bank's responsible parties to repay debts in full," the whole venue erupted in thunderous applause and cheers. Subsequently, it was decided to elect fifteen representatives to be responsible for negotiations. After the representatives were elected, the attendees firmly requested the representatives to take an oath, followed by a three-bow salute, to show the public's expectations and the importance of their entrustment.

Meeting Details: The presidium of the meeting consisted of Zhang Zilian, Chen Zhonggao, Hong Yanbin, Qiu Liangyu, Jiang Beiping, and others. Following formalities, Chairman Zhang Zilian and others reported that since the sudden closure of the Ningshi Bank, there has been no news of resumption of business or liquidation. To protect the legal rights of creditors and facilitate negotiations, the creditors' association was formed, and registration was initiated. Within a week, 2,358 households registered, totaling 513,467.98 yuan. The majority of creditors are small business owners, whose hard-earned money has been lost, a truly pitiful situation. Today's meeting was convened with enthusiastic participation, and we will discuss appropriate measures for further action, demanding full repayment. It was also found that the bank's liabilities amount to over 700,000 yuan. Although the person in charge has gone into hiding, we should appeal to society and ensure the achievement of our goal.

Election of Representatives: After discussion, the following fifteen representatives were elected to be responsible for negotiations: Zhang Zilian, Chen Zhonggao, Wang Beiping, Qiu Xubai, Wang Xiangqing, Hong Yanbin, Qiu Liangyu, Wu Peng, Zhou Kechuan, Zhu Shujian, Tong Xinqin, Wang Hongzhai, Chen Yuantong, Zhao Kuiyi, Xiao Chuhua. He hoped that everyone would await the results quietly during the process and not cause any twists and turns due to resentment. The representatives will act in good conscience and work hard to stabilize society. If there is any malfeasance, they will be "traitors." The meeting ended with laughter and cheers from the entire venue.

Common Sense Consultation

Shanghai Municipal Public Knowledge Guidance Committee Legal and Medical Common Sense Consultation Rules: (1) These rules are formulated in accordance with Articles 10 and 11 of the committee's articles of association; (2) Citizens of this city may apply to the committee for consultation on legal and medical common sense matters; (3) The consultation methods are divided into oral and written. For oral consultation, they must come to the committee in person (Confucius Temple Park) and fill out a consultation form. Those who are illiterate will have the form filled out by the committee staff. For written consultation, the details of the matter must be clearly stated, and the real name and latest mailing address must be signed; (4) After receiving the consultation form or request letter, the committee will immediately ask the specially appointed lawyers and doctors to be responsible for answering it; (5) The committee's reply to citizens regarding legal and medical common sense consultation matters will not be later than one week from the date of receipt; (6) The committee is purely for social service and does not charge any fees; (7) When necessary, the committee may introduce lawyers and doctors to interview the applicant, but the lawyers and doctors are voluntary and do not charge the parties any fees; (8) At the end of each month, the committee may compile and publish the citizens' legal common sense consultation matters, but citizens who do not wish to disclose their real names and mailing addresses may state the matter in advance, and the committee will act accordingly; (9) When necessary, the committee may set up consultation offices in various districts; (10) The committee's legal and medical common sense consultation time, for oral consultation, is temporarily set from 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM every day, and for written consultation, it is not limited to this; (11) If there are any matters not covered in these rules, they may be amended; (12) These rules will be implemented after being passed by the committee members.

Radio Broadcast Guidance

Shanghai Municipal Public Knowledge Guidance Committee Wireless Broadcasting Guidance Method: (1) This committee implements wireless broadcasting guidance for the purpose of imparting common knowledge to the public; (2) This committee temporarily uses ×× radio station as the broadcasting location; (3) The broadcasting scope is based on the items stipulated in Article 9 of the committee's articles of association; (4) The broadcasting time is temporarily set to × times per week, held on × afternoon, from × to × hours; (5) The broadcasting personnel will be rotated by the committee members. When necessary, experts from all walks of life may be invited to give lectures; (6) The broadcasting personnel should submit the broadcasting materials to the committee for editing and publication; (7) If the committee's methods are not comprehensive, they may be revised at any time; (8) These methods will be implemented after being passed by the committee members.

Bandit Captured at the New Gate Bridge; Hostage Rescued in Pudong; Four-Year-Old Child in Bandit's Den for Over a Month; Over 20 Kidnappers to Be Sent to Court This Morning 148

Li Guanlin, a local resident of an unmarked bungalow on Route雷上达 in the French Concession, is over fifty years old. His only son, nicknamed Jinsheng, is only four years old. At around 7:00 PM on the 13th of last month, four bandits suddenly came, kidnapped Jinsheng, and took him away. Before leaving, they fired a shot from a handgun, fortunately without injuring anyone. However, a month has passed since and there has been no news. Yesterday afternoon, the French police safely rescued the hostage Li Jinsheng in the area of 交新沙 in Pudong, and arrested the kidnappers and suspects. The details are investigated separately below:

Negotiation of Location

After the bandits kidnapped Jinsheng, they repeatedly sent letters demanding a large ransom, without specifying an address. The day before yesterday (the 19th), Guanlin was replied to, stating that tomorrow (the 20th) at 2:00 PM in the afternoon, someone must wear a blue cloth long shirt, holding a sugar cane, and wait at the New Gate Bridge. At that time, someone will come to negotiate.

Three Captured

After receiving the letter, Li Guanlin reported to the Lujiawan Police Station. The police chief ordered Inspector Jin Jiulin, detective Zhang Ziying, Zhou Buguang, Deputy Detective Qin Youyu, and detective Dai Rongji to disguise themselves and rush to the area. Before long, three people came forward to negotiate. The detectives immediately stepped forward and captured them all in one fell swoop. According to them, the three are named Dong Aqing, Chen Qingsheng, and Zhao Taotao, local residents. The hostage is hidden in the area of 交新沙 in Pudong.

Hostage Rescued

After the French police received the confession, they urgently ordered the original team of detectives to escort Dong Aqing and others across the river to Pudong. They first went to the 3rd District Sub-bureau in Pudong for assistance. Sub-bureau chief Zhang ordered several detectives to assist in the destination. The hostage was then rescued, and the bandits Su Shaogen and Yang Hongde, who were guarding the hostage, were arrested on the spot. Afterwards, over 20 suspects were arrested in Fuxing Inn on Beller Road, Yangshupu, and Ziyang Road, and detained in the French police station. They will be sent to court for interrogation this morning.

Domestic Pigment Industry Shortens the Credit Period for Selling Goods Due to Tightening of Finances and Reduction of Loans; One-Month Promissory Notes Are All Changed to Ten Days 149

According to the China News Agency, the domestic pigment industry in this city has recently adopted a tight fiscal policy and reduced external loans. Therefore, the association held a meeting to discuss it. Everyone agreed that the strength of the industry is limited, and it is difficult to trade on credit. The credit period for selling loans has been revised. The details are as follows:

Full Agreement

A few days ago, the members of the Municipal Domestic Pigment Industry Association, including Xie Ji Xin, Tong Ren He, Jin Tai Chang, De Tai Cheng, Tong Xie Xiang, Tong Tai Xiang, Jiu He Xiang, Tai He Xiang, Yi Yu Chang, Cheng Mao, Yong Mao Xiang, Fuxing Heng, Tong Yuan Sheng, Tong Chang Xiang, Hui Chang, Run Chang Xiang, Tong He Xiang, Xie Mao Xiang, and other 20 companies, recently decided to revise the credit period for selling goods due to the reduction of loans in the financial sector and limited strength.

Reduced to Ten Days

All members agreed that the credit period for selling goods to customers in various places was originally divided into two types: cash and one-month term. Except for cash transactions that do not need to be changed, all one-month term notes will be changed to ten-day term notes from today, both locally and abroad. Overdue will be rejected, and all members have been notified to inform all customers at home and abroad.

Various Textile Mills Advocate the Use of Domestic Cotton; Foreign Cotton Sales Decline Daily; It Is Predicted That This Year's Sales Will Be at Most One Million Bales; Shaanxi Cotton Is Difficult to Sell Due to Merchants' Speculation 150

In recent years, textile mills in this city have actively used domestic cotton, and imports of foreign cotton have decreased daily. According to news from the cotton industry yesterday, since the establishment of the Cotton Industry Improvement Society of the National Economic Commission, the output of cotton in our country has increased year by year, and the quality has become increasingly better. Therefore, various textile mills are happy to adopt it in large quantities, and sales are increasing by leaps and bounds. It is found that during the period of 1920-21, foreign cotton sales were very strong, with an annual volume of 4.5 to 6 million bales. From 1922-23, the sales volume was only 3 million bales, and last year, the sales volume was only 1.8 million bales. This year's sales volume, according to observations in the cotton industry, will not exceed 1 million bales at most. The most imported cotton is from the United States, followed by India, and then Egypt. It is heard that the sales volume of domestic cotton is more brisk this month than last month. The rumor that Shaanxi cotton is difficult to sell is due to the speculation of a few merchants and is not the whole situation.
