Page 15

Free Talk

Gogol's Words on Character Description 231

— Gu Ding

In Gogol’s "The Overcoat," when writing about a character other than the protagonist Akaky Akakievich, he suddenly inserts this passage:

"Of course, there is no need to say much about this tailor, but since he has been mentioned, in order to fully and clearly describe the character of each person in the novel, there is no way but to talk about him here."

After introducing the tailor in a few sentences, when writing about the tailor's wife, he says:

"Since we have mentioned his wife, we must also say a few words about her."

This made me think a lot. Because when I read it at the time, it seemed like I had this feeling: this work is undoubtedly good; but in a work, when introducing characters, is it good to insert the author's "novel writing method" or similar opinions, and would this affect the integrity of the work? Of course, Gogol's era is far from us, and perhaps he had some feelings at the time that made him have to write that way; but when we read it now, we always feel that there is a need for research. After thinking for a while, it seemed that there was no result; however, it gave me another kind of inspiration: that is, Gogol's valuable opinions on writing novels. Now when I read his "Dead Souls," that opinion makes me see a very clear outline. At the beginning of "Chapter Two," he writes about the protagonist Chichikov's servants like this:

"It wouldn't be too much trouble to introduce the two servants of our main character to the reader here. Of course, they are not important figures, only so-called second- or third-rate people, and they have nothing to do with the backbone and significant development of this epic poem, at most touching it a little, or mentioning it briefly; -- but the author likes to be meticulous in everything..."

Therefore, it makes me think that most beginners often make such a mistake when writing: that is, they fail to describe the appearance and character of each character in the work--whether important or unimportant--in detail or briefly; they are always impatient and only care about the rapid development of the story, so that many characters are just written with a name and that's it. As a result, of course, it is easy to make people feel as if they are reading a "news chronicle" instead of a work of art. To cure this problem, I think Gogol's words are indeed the right medicine.

This is not all. Gogol further gives us more practical hints in "Dead Souls":

"Manilov then led his friend into the house. Passing through the gate, the front hall, and the dining room, although very quickly, we want to use this very short time, whether it can be done naturally is not certain, to talk about a few words about this owner. However, the author should state that such a plan is very difficult. It is easier to describe a character with a large stage. Here, we can only smear the paint on the canvas like this--shining black eyes, thick eyebrows, deep wrinkles on the forehead, and a black or blood-red coat solemnly draped over the shoulders--the small portrait is painted; however, such gentlemen who are everywhere and look very similar. Because we are used to seeing them, they probably all have some subtle, elusive characteristics--it is very difficult to draw portraits of these people. If you want these subtle, subtle characteristics to be in front of your eyes, you must pay special attention and use the eyes trained in identifying people to deeply shoot into the bottom of the spirit of people."

The last few sentences of this passage are very important. He paints a character for us to see; but he immediately points out that this is still not enough. The important thing is: to put those "subtle, elusive characteristics in front of your eyes," "and use the eyes trained in identifying people to deeply shoot into the bottom of the spirit of people."

Life 232

— Li Sanlang

Lying on the bed, the damaged canvas bed always crackles and pops incessantly, seemingly casting an odd shadow, stirring my weary mind, exhausted from the day's toil for life, a chaos of terrors. It's as if tragedy flickers in a rapidly moving film, scene after scene, now joyous, now painful, now tearful. It seems life has given me only terrifying shadows. Even when I climbed from the treacherous mountain paths to level ground, believing I could stride peacefully toward a beautiful countryside, that may have been just a dream. But as a child, I had many beautiful and lovely dreams, dreams of how great my future would be, dreams of my infinite happiness. Now, all of that has completely disappeared. Not only is there no chance to dream of the future, but life doesn't even let me dream. It seems even the courage to dream has vanished. Isn't that so? I descended from the high and dangerous mountain paths, and on the tranquil ground, I thought I could live peacefully. But this era is no longer so simple or ordinary. Before long, I felt that the tranquil environment was not really tranquil. In an instant, ahead was no longer flat land, but another terrifying mountain range, a boundless sea of raging waves, and the pangs of hunger and cold would once again descend upon me, the traveler. Thus, I must struggle again, hoping the sunlight will illuminate the earth, and I can slowly find my way in the middle. I must climb over dense mountain ranges, or encounter a raging ocean. I must find a light boat to cross the sea, drifting and drifting, crossing the terrifying ocean again.

And so, I constantly, every moment, tread this never-ending path of ups and downs, all for the sake of life, to avoid the whip of hunger and cold lashing me relentlessly. So, is there still the courage and opportunity to dream as I did in childhood?

Therefore, when I lie down on the canvas bed that is as awkward as I am, its old and torn crackling sounds seem to deliberately warn me, or imploringly sigh. However, because this journey has given me the taste of hunger and cold to a very deep degree, and after my constant running and jumping, I get this chance to lie down, lying on the damaged canvas bed, what mood do I have to care about its unfortunate situation? Of course, I treat its broken, sighing crackling sound as mixed in with my nightly life. The more I toss and turn, the more I cannot sleep peacefully, the more it crackles and pops incessantly. Of course, when it no longer has the strength to hold me up, I lie down on the cement floor.

Lying on the cement floor is the same as lying on the damaged canvas bed. I am always thinking about the day's running around, thinking about how to avoid hunger and cold. However, the ground is silent, with no echoing sound.

Tomorrow, I must once again climb the high mountain, drifting across the ocean with an empty heart.

Early Summer 233

— Wei Zhongtian

Green fields, green sky, green branches, green sky...

Spring has long since gone so far away, spring has left this green world, everywhere is a patch of emerald green, a patch of azure blue, if not thinking about the burden of life is getting heavier day by day, this scenery will always make people a little happy.

The early summer breeze stirs up so many of my memories, these memories, half are lovable, half are hateful. ...

Since summer came to Tokyo, there have been two things that attract attention in society, that is, women's umbrellas and paper fans. Japanese women's umbrellas are really very particular, there are red ones, green ones, patterned ones, purple-blue ones, all kinds of things. I have never seen them before, I believe some people see these umbrellas, maybe they will associate with the beauty of women's youth. The June sun shines on the girl under the red umbrella, seems more beautiful, many people say, Japan's beautiful girls are too many.

As for that paper fan is also very particular, and small, and exquisite, looks always feel a special flavor. -- exotic flavor.

The early summer breeze makes people a little tired, making people feel the length of the day, the fatigue of life. In Shanghai, it must be very hot at this moment, but the weather is not hot in Tokyo, the wind is still so gentle across your face, did not think of the summer is terrible. Now the cicadas have not yet, but the mosquitoes are more and more every day.

Foreign Lady 234

Hygienic Stinky Tofu 235

— Liu Shi

Perhaps my tastes are a bit low, but I remember that those who have been to "Autumn Moon over the Calm Lake" always exaggerate the deliciousness of the spiced dried tofu sold there, but I don't feel that way. I can't taste its so-called "deliciousness." Perhaps it's because I didn't pair it with a cup of real Longjing tea, didn't open a pot of "Nine Creeks and Eighteen Gorges" water, and didn't have an ancient porcelain cup! No! Not only do I lack these things, but I probably also lack a bright and clean window like Mr. Zhitang's Bitter Rain Studio, a leisurely pastoral heart, and two or three connoisseurs who can taste tea and distinguish flavors! Eating, for us common people, is mostly just filling our stomachs. The taste and smell of our tongues are probably less capable than those of refined people. Therefore, the dried tofu that I love to eat is actually a kind of stinky tofu that can be bought on the streets every day. Spend two coppers, stand by the oil pot, use a bamboo skewer to pick a piece into the pot, add a little spicy sauce, and send it hot into my mouth, I feel very appetizing. If I have one or two silver coins in my pocket, buy ten or eight pieces and bring them home for dinner, wouldn't that be the ultimate delicacy for the poor? As for whether it is hygienic or not, I have never examined it, because I have eaten it for half my life, but I have never suffered any serious illness, so I will unscientifically assume that it does not harm hygiene! Yes, before I have the good fortune to go to "Autumn Moon over the Calm Lake," and before I have the leisurely mood to carefully chew spiced hygienic dried tofu, let's not overthrow those stinky tofu stalls for the time being! That's how I personally think.

However, these stinky tofu stalls may offend the noses of people with "high-class tastes," which is not surprising.

Mr. Zhitang compares "the scientific essays that are clamoring today" to "so-called hygienic stinky tofu." This is to say that stinky tofu is inherently unhygienic, and now adding the word "hygienic" is a contradictory humor, isn't it? But why not think that Mr. Zhitang is opposed to scientific essays, just as Mr. Zhitang is not opposed to dried tofu. What Mr. Zhitang opposes is only "what is clamoring today." He admires Wilde's "Natural History of Selborne," Fabre's "Souvenirs Entomologiques," and Thomson's "Secrets of Animal Life" very much, and laments that "it cannot be found in that "Siku Quanshu", it is truly rare and precious." "If we want to see some scientific essays, we still have to borrow from foreign countries for the time being." Is it difficult to say that Mr. Zhitang is still opposed to scientific essays? Yes, the same dried tofu, some can be used for elegant people to taste tea, and some can be used to fill the stomachs of hungry people. What Mr. Zhitang opposes is clearly the kind of scientific essays that cannot be used for discussion in the Bitter Rain Studio, which is also clear.

"I don't know what so-called scientific essays are. According to me, this should be something that dreams of science and has the dream of writing." Although this generally seems to explain something, it is actually vague. Scientific essays, in today's sense, cannot be such an abstract thing. If it is a scientific explanation of the practice of observation, or a fragment of scientific writing, then, in order to express the scientific truth fully, the language must be popular and have the appealing literary quality of a work of art. Therefore, although Fabre's and Thomson's masterpieces are worthy of being respected as spiced hygienic dried tofu, in today's China, objectively speaking, they are only things for scholars to discuss or for authors to study, and cannot fill the empty stomachs on the streets. The scientific essays currently needed cannot borrow from others' light, but must use scientific laws to explain the phenomena that are pressing down on everyone's heads. These observations, which are pressing us tightly, belong to society, so even if things that specifically write about the lives of insects and animals are beautiful, they are only tea snacks, not a main meal. "Why does a scholar who has painted a few strokes of ink plum blossoms" necessarily "go and write about famous paintings of the Renaissance"? Can't Chinese scientific essays rely on their own practice to create?

As for saying that people who are not scientists like Fabre and do not have such writing skills "should refrain from moving their honorable hands," isn't this clearly canceling people's efforts? I am not going to accept this. It's pitiful to say that the so-called "scientific essays that are clamoring today" are still in their infancy, and there are no good products, but it is also a fact, but the trend clearly shows that they are growing. Because the practice of life has determined its development, whether in content or form, it cannot become the spiced tofu for elegant scholars to taste tea in the Bitter Rain Studio, so it can only be temporarily regarded as "stinky tofu" and sold on the streets! Therefore, Mr. Zhitang's satire on us is not considered harsh or unbearable. Instead, it takes off the noble coat of scientific essays.

Can things sold on the streets be unprepared for hygiene? That's not true. Stinky tofu is, after all, a satirical metaphor. What scientific essayists must guard against is having toxins, not only should we be careful about the stinky, but also pay attention to the fragrant and sweet! Fragrant things can also be poisonous. Therefore, adding the word "hygienic" to stinky tofu is really wonderfully like soy sauce.

University Days (8) 236

— Written by German author Storm, translated by Chen Yinzhi

At this moment, I discovered that Nellie was wearing a set of light-colored wool clothes with flowers tonight. Like the previous one, this set was probably also taken from the mayor's wife's closet, because last winter, the mayor's wife's broad chest and copper-purple complexion, matched with this set of colored rose clothes, actually caused others to feel a little funny. But now this style is just in vogue; the bright and dark-skinned girl's face matches this set of clothes very well.

After the "Mazurka" was over, Nellie let her head and thin arms droop again, and I sent her to her seat. Fritz and Charlotte had also just come out of the dance floor and were sitting near us. Just at this moment, Mrs. Polica also came over with cakes and tea; she did not speak to her daughter, but gave her a smiling and proud look, as if to show that she would serve her tea and cakes after serving them to that noble lady. The noble lady had been looking at these two mothers and daughters for a while with her unique lazy expression. "Your daughter is very beautiful tonight, Mrs. Polica!" she said, while putting sugar in her teacup.

The complimented lady bowed humbly, "Thank you, miss, this is also thanks to the mayor's wife's care."

"Oh ha! — So that's how it is! That set of rose clothes!" She then cast a long glance at Nellie. Nellie wanted to look back at her, but her eyes were already dim; I saw how a pair of tears rolled down her cheeks.

Charlotte seemed not to have seen it; her attention turned to the open doorway: I was taken aback, because I saw the French tailor's yellow face also appearing among the spectators in the crowd. He seemed to be very happy, and the snuffbox was being turned over and over in his hand. His black eyes looked happily into the hall.

"Is that your father, Miss Nellie?" Charlotte said, pointing outside the door.

Rena Li looked out and couldn't help but tremble all over. "Mother!" she shouted, unconsciously grabbing the arm of the old lady who was still serving guests in front of us.

Mrs. Polica also saw her husband, who was so happy that he was gesticulating, at this time, and she was not happy, but she cheered up. "He came from the inn," she said, "He came to see you dance."

Nellie walked towards the door, and I unconsciously followed her; when she approached the door, the mayor had already walked to her father and invited him into the hall for a glass of sugar wine. But the tailor refused to move. "Thank you, I am your loyal servant, Mr. Mayor!" he said, while bending his back and taking a step back. "I wish I could be like my grandfather, who served in the court of Louis XVI! I know my place very well!"

Supplement to Shen Bao

Talking Points

Banning the "Cherish Paper" Associations 237

— Chen

Recently, the China Paperboard Manufacturers Association submitted a report to the Jiangsu Provincial Government, requesting the ban of "Cherish Paper" associations in various places. This report, coming from the mouths of business operators, naturally speaks of the great principle of "eliminating bad habits and cherishing material resources." Perhaps it also contains a lot of "business acumen," but "respecting and cherishing written paper," in itself, is a kind of "fetishism" and should have been criticized by people long ago. It is only because of a strange idea that has always existed in our country, that square characters are the relics of sages, and all people who are "scholarly and of the same flesh and blood" should respect, cherish, and pray to them, otherwise they would blaspheme the sages and be condemned by Heaven. The "characters," a linguistic tool created by Cangjie in the past, could not have anticipated that they would be regarded by later "scholars" as something that could "suppress demons and ward off evil."

Besides trying their best to quibble over words in order to show off their mysteriousness, "respecting and cherishing written paper" is also one of their actual practices. Looking at how "scholars" of the past treated written paper, they not only could not throw it away anywhere, but also had to gather it together and burn it, and throw the ashes into the sea. This was definitely not for cleanliness and hygiene, but was actually no different from the secretive behavior of people of "heretical ways and odd methods" who manipulated their own incantations and seals. The former "deceives the public with false words," while the latter dazzles fools with his own knowledge.

The report from the China Paperboard Manufacturers Association allows us to see that there is still such a latent force in our society. The government's ban on them is indeed a happy event for eliminating old customs and superstitions, but we also have a further wish, which is how to find a way to break the superstitions of a small number of "scholars," because history shows us that this strange thing not only produces many evils, but also has a not small relationship with the country and the nation.

Eyeglasses 238

— Ge Bai

It seems that a movie star was the first to wear sunglasses in public places, but now fashionable women each have a pair, which has become a common phenomenon. In Shanghai, movie stars always take the lead in fashion, and wearing sunglasses is a fashionable trend.

Reading Suzhou ballad novels, I know that the Chinese have long had something called "single lenses." Nowadays, British ladies have changed to using "double lenses" instead. That kind of way of looking at people always lacks generosity. However, changing them into the style of eyeglasses, the nose and ears are initially subjected to a kind of unexpected restraint. Moreover, when someone suddenly pops out from the side street, looking at them through the edge of the glasses, it's almost like a Mount Tai pressing down, often leading to a bit of helplessness. I myself unfortunately suffer from extreme nearsightedness. I remember when I was in middle school, my seat gradually moved from the back row to the front row, but the words on the blackboard were always so distant. I had to squint my eyelids into a line to make out a blurry outline. I had long refused to get a pair of glasses. Many of my classmates wore glasses, but I never wanted my nose and ears to be clamped by that kind of hard thing. Later, a science teacher gave a very detailed explanation about the eyeballs. Worried about going blind in the future, I secretly got a pair, but still put them in my pocket after class. This was because there was an even bigger reason involved.

At that time, wearing glasses was considered fashionable. Anyone who had read chapter novels would never forget that when a suave young man appeared on stage, the author would at least write about a pair of gold-rimmed glasses on his face. Even in the "Tale of Laughter and Tears," which was popular for a time, it is said that the author even used a pair of glasses and a fountain pen as foreshadowing for Fengxi's change of heart. Wouldn't I be worried about being a romantic figure myself when this beautiful ornament was discovered on my nose? Moreover, classmates would never let you go, asking you with a special attitude, "Are you wearing glasses?" clearly mocking you for trying to be fashionable. Then, after sacrificing my nose and ears, and also sweating on my back, wouldn't it be a happy thing to see a little less? Moreover, the highest secret of the art of living is to not see and not ask! As for finally putting them on my nose later, it was truly unspeakable pain. Initially, when I couldn't see things, I could squint my eyelids. After borrowing the power of that concave glass to help with my insufficient eyeballs, even when I thought I could see very clearly before, I couldn't help but take them out of my pocket and put them on my nose, hoping to see even more clearly. Over time, it became a habit. When people asked me, "Are you wearing glasses?" I could interpret it as a question of sympathy, and I would naturally answer calmly, "Nearsighted!"

However, whether it's Tolick, Crookes, or glass lenses, they are always white. When teachers wore sunglasses during exams, they were inevitably cursed by students as "cruel ghosts." Fortune tellers wear dark glasses, and everyone knows they are blind, while new brides are recognized as having this right. In the past, young girls were shy, and when so many people were teasing the newlyweds in the bridal chamber, she could borrow two pieces of black glass to avoid those frivolous gazes. The sales of other sunglasses were minimal.

Last summer, I learned from advertisements about an invention called mirror-outside-mirror. The most sensational words in the advertisement were that it could "protect the eyes." But first, close your eyes and think: wearing glasses in the summer is already the most painful thing. If one pair is not enough, and you put on another pair, even if your nose and ears are not afraid of sacrifice, wouldn't it be too much trouble when sweat drips down from your forehead? Although my own eyeballs are not up to par, this kind of well-intentioned compulsion seems too much!

Now that sunglasses are all the rage, because I don't want to spend extra money to get a pair of sunglasses with the same degree of nearsightedness, I don't agree that this is the only way to avoid strong sunlight, unless it's to be fashionable, of course.

Burglary 239

— Ping

The high cost of housing in Shanghai seems to be self-evident. Although nine out of ten houses are empty now, rental prices still refuse to "drop and sell cheaply." As a result, the so-called "Shikumen" houses are filled with people like pigsties. As a low-income earner, I am undoubtedly a patron of those pigsties. However, that old Western-style suit that maintains the special life of our gentry class always receives unusual attention from the cohabitants. This contains two meanings. One is jealousy, which makes me extremely ashamed. Although in this big city, a person's weight is distinguished by the high or low of their clothes, a group living in a pigsty is like being naked in a bathhouse, with everyone showing their parents' pure bodies, regardless of status. The other—to put it a bit too much—perhaps is greed? In fact, it also comes from envy and jealousy. Human beings are inherently endowed with an upward-striving heart. An old joke once told us that a beggar hoped to become an emperor. The only difference is that some climb upward step by step, while others want to ascend to heaven in one step. Those in the pigsty group naturally belong to the latter category. In that case, the gentry class in their ideals is worthy of being envied and then coveted. However, what makes me uneasy day and night is in these two gazes. On the one hand, I have been squeezed into the noble class. On the other hand, I have fantasized that perhaps something unfavorable will happen. As a result, it is indeed nervous oversensitivity, and the desire to move is becoming increasingly urgent.

I started asking friends for help, because it is too unlikely to find a new hope for my ideal safe haven from "rental advertisements." Fellow members of the gentry class might be able to help. Half a month ago, I moved into such a satisfactory new home. The new residence is a large house, in short, it is above all ordinary Shikumen houses, and is directly rented from the main landlord. The rental price, with one less middleman's profit, does not make me suffer too much. It is a spacious wing room, facing south, with sunlight and air all in excellent condition. In addition, the careful security of the doors and all the telephone equipment make me feel that I have climbed up a level.

However, unfavorable things did happen in the new residence. One morning, when I was about to get dressed, I found that my glasses, cards, and all sorts of trivial notes had been moved from my pockets to the hat rack beside the clothes rack. The newest of my three Western-style suits had disappeared without a trace.

Page 18

After this news spread, the cohabitants said in unison: "Nothing has been stolen here for decades!" I have full trust in these words. The friend of the introducer mentioned this when he recommended the new residence. But the sudden theft on that day after decades seems to be related to my destiny.

The losses totaled a new Western-style suit, a Parker fountain pen, and four or five yuan in cash. He carefully placed my most important nearsighted glasses and an insurance policy on the hat rack. If I were to replace them all at once now, it would cost as much as sixty yuan.

At that time, there was a lot of discussion and surprise about this first-time theft. Fortunately, I didn't want to investigate, otherwise I would inevitably reveal my own sourness. Moreover, many people who had nothing to do with me were uneasy all day long. At this point, I couldn't help but look at fate with disbelief. I initially wanted to jump out of the pigsty group. First, I was ashamed of being seen as part of the noble class. Second, I was afraid that poorer people would have the idea of turning me into a pauper. I harbored a despicable heart first, and this theft seems to be self-inflicted. Or perhaps it is retribution. What more can I say?

The Chauffeur 240

— Jingfu

The vast twilight slowly enveloped everything. In the quiet and elegant garden, the flowers and trees gently and serenely swayed. The tall and graceful Western-style building surrounded by flowers and trees quietly sank into silence, surrounded by an atmosphere of sweet warmth. But Ah Fu, the chauffeur of that brand-new black car in the country, had just watched his masters, that gathering of husband, wife, and children, with their tender words and smiles, and intimate holding of hands, get out of the car and walk with light steps, like happy little birds, flashing into the house to spend that festive night. For a long time, he stood there in a daze. His sore and weak hands silently gripped the steering wheel. His sunken gaze was filled with endless sorrow and melancholy.

The cool breeze of the summer evening gently rose, brushing past the lightly swaying flowers and trees, and blowing against his chest. He couldn't help but feel his heart tremble and beat wildly. The gentle and cool breeze is most sweet and comfortable for those happy people, but for Ah Fu, it only stirred up his mood.

The happy shadows of the masters floated up, and immediately reflected the desolate image of his own house, the thin, haggard, and worried face of his wife, making his heart feel as if it were pressed by a heavy stone, and his mind was stabbed by even more things—rent, food money, creditors for small debts, and so on. Moreover, tonight is supposed to be a happy festive occasion! People are all going home to celebrate, leaving behind a wife who is lonely and cold, and who might be complaining and crying, leaving behind his own heart, which is so painful and anxious.

"Why don't they ever pay you your salary? One month, two months, three months! Why are you so muddle-headed? Those rich people, do they really lack those few coins of yours? Think for yourself, and let us, mother and son, starve... Alas, are you dead?... Why don't you ask them for it?... Hmph, afraid you'll take it to the brothel!" And his wife's heartless voice, filled with crying and scolding, whipped at his heart, making him even angrier! God knows, how could those rich people be short a few coins from their chauffeur's salary? It's been three months since they paid. His wife even complains, thinking that he took the money to visit prostitutes! When Ah Fu thought of these things, the hand gripping the steering wheel kept pressing against his chest, as if his chest were about to burst open.

"How could they lack those few coins?" This also made him think of the situation today when he went to the big hospital to pick up the young master. The young master was skipping school, saying that his throat was a little uncomfortable. Only then did he know! He didn't know how he was treated, but after staying in the hospital for five days, the master handed over a check for one thousand yuan. The two dogs of the mistress, one medical treatment cost seventy or eighty yuan. Ah Fu's three months of hard work were not worth that much! And they haven't paid him a single penny. Today, he mustered up his courage, and when the master returned the seventy-five yuan veterinary fee, he boldly opened his mouth, but the master looked at him a little unhappily: "I don't have any change, ask the mistress, I don't care about these trivial things!" He endured this nail and swallowed it. In the afternoon, he waited for a long time and couldn't find an opportunity to talk to the mistress. Until the guests left, the mistress was busy with her own evening dress and organizing clothes for the young master, instructing the nanny to do this and that. Ah Fu secretly went in and said softly to the mistress: "Mistress, lend me a few..." The mistress didn't wait for him to finish speaking and turned her head to shout at him: "What?" It stunned him! Then he stammered: "Please, mistress, lend me some money." The mistress seemed very annoyed. "Tomorrow!"

Another tomorrow, forcing him to retreat, still falling into the burning and frantic chaos. The joyful festive scene in the Western-style building only made him more uneasy...

The Struggle of Pilsudski (Part 1) 242

— Nan

The death of Polish national hero General Józef Piłsudski aroused worldwide condolences. The General's great personality and his spirit of hard struggle for the nation and people are indeed worthy of human admiration. At 10:30 a.m. on the 3rd of this month, Nanjing Central University specially invited Mr. Władysław Mazurkiewicz, the Polish Minister to China, to speak about the life of General Piłsudski during the Prime Minister's Memorial Week. Mr. Mazurkiewicz has the attitude of a scholar and has many exchanges with the academic community in our country. The friendship between China and Poland is built on culture and scholarship, so it becomes more and more intimate. This, of course, must be attributed to the efforts of Minister Mazurkiewicz. Now, the main points of Minister Mazurkiewicz's speech are recorded, because our country's current environment needs all citizens to struggle and strive for freedom and revival. General Piłsudski's life is our best model. The main points of the Polish envoy's speech are: I feel that this coincidence is a rare opportunity to give a speech during Dr. Sun Yat-Sen's Memorial Week, because these two great men in the East and West have extremely similar points in their life, achievements, success, and doctrine. Both sacrificed their lives for their country, and both started to struggle to transform their country from a young age, making continuous efforts. At the same time, both were loved by the people of their countries to the highest degree. General Józef Piłsudski was the transformer of Poland and the teacher of the entire Polish nation. What I am talking about today is a condensed picture of the General's lifelong struggle, his endless difficulties, and countless obstacles, which ultimately created the General of today.

The childhood environment has the greatest impact on the success of people's life careers. When the General was young, he witnessed Poland suffering all kinds of tragic oppression from foreign tribes, and even could not freely speak the Polish national language. The General's father was even a sincere patriotic man, who participated in the 1863 revolutionary independence movement several years before the General was born. Therefore, his family was filled with the highest and most loyal patriotic spirit. The General was fully influenced and built a very solid foundation for future success. When the General first entered elementary school, the school forced them to speak Russian and did not allow them to use Polish. In the years he spent in school, he planted the seedling of the General's restoration of the ancestral homeland. When he grew up and entered university, he secretly organized political groups with a small number of Polish classmates and began to actually resist Imperial Russia, the oppressor of Poland. The General's patriotism was so eager that he did not consider the difficulties and dangers of the future at first. Before long, the General was finally expelled from the university for being anti-Russian. This was the first difficulty the General encountered, but the General's spirit was not discouraged. He still worked hard for freedom and actively advanced on the most difficult road, urgently returning to his hometown of Vilnius to gather young comrades and give them ideological training, and actively carrying out revolutionary work. He was even more hated by the Russian government. Soon he was arrested and sentenced to five years of imprisonment, exiled to Siberia. The Tsarist Russia ruled Poland for one hundred and twenty-five years, and thousands of Polish patriots were exiled to Siberia one after another. At that time, the General was only a young man in his twenties.

The World Peace Association, for the purpose of promoting peace efforts, broadcasts peace issues every Wednesday from 3:00 PM to 4:00 PM at the shipping radio station, lectured by the Secretary-General Sun Xiangzhong (孫翔仲). His lectures are concise and insightful, deeply appreciated by the audience. Mr. Sun went to Pingjin (平晋) last month to visit Mr. Duan Zhengyuan (段正元), resulting in the interruption of the broadcast. Recently, the association received letters from various circles at home and abroad, requesting Mr. Sun to continue his broadcasts. The association, considering the importance of its mission for peace, could not refuse and resumed broadcasting yesterday. The topic of his lecture was "The Dividing Line Between Harming the Country and Saving the Country (禍國與救國之分界綫)." He will provide a detailed explanation of the dividing line between political, military, and other proposals for promoting new culture and old morality, which aim to save the country but may mistakenly harm the country.

Movie News

"The Old Dark House" Screening 246

"Zombies" and "vampires" are at least phenomena unacceptable in the scientifically advanced 20th century, but there are many exceptions in the universe. We must use reason to observe, explore, and experiment with these metaphysical forces. At the same time, we can also draw conclusions about whether "zombies" can absorb human essence and how to eliminate this harm. "The Old Dark House (古屋奇案)," now showing in Nanjing (南京), is a unique masterpiece by MGM, breaking all horror film records on the screen. It is the most successful and greatest supernatural creation of director Tod Browning, who once directed the banned film "Dracula (殭屍)," and lead actor Bela Lugosi. The original author is Guy Endore, who wrote "The Werewolf of Paris (巴黎人狼)," a book that caused a great stir in the philosophical and literary circles. In addition to Lugosi, the actors include Lionel Barrymore, Elizabeth Allan, Melvyn Douglas, and Raymond Hatton, all of whom are prominent stars. Especially Carroll Borland, who plays the female vampire Luna, has a sinister and terrifying appearance. The background lighting and atmosphere are chilling. The cinematographer is Huang Zongzhan, the only Chinese technician in Hollywood, and the film is accompanied by the latest masterpiece "Fra Diavolo (詐死)" by the comedic duo Laurel and Hardy. The picture on the left is a scene from the film.

"Forgotten Faces" Soon to be Released 247

Columbia's new film "Forgotten Faces (慾海遺恨)" is a significant creation in the world of cinema. With the theme of urban diseases, it writes about the dangers of sexual life, giving a profound stimulus to urban youth, pointing out the lost path on one hand, and exposing the pathological conditions and revealing the location of the disease without omission, truly a compassionate and meritorious work for the world and people's hearts, and will be released soon at the New Kwong Ta Theatre (新光大戲院).

News Regarding the Performance of "A Doll's House" 248

Nora's Great Fortune

This year can be said to be the year of "Nora (娜拉)". There have been more than six thousand records of the play being performed in various places. Many famous figures in the drama and film circles have also decided to perform this script. It is said that they have been secretly rehearsing for more than two months and will premiere it at the Jin Cheng Theatre (金城) at the end of this month.

The Actors of "Nora"

Speaking of the actors of "Nora", they are all well-known figures. Zhao Dan (趙丹), Jin Shan (金山), and Wei Heling (魏鶴齡) are all figures in the drama and film circles most welcomed by the audience. Ms. Lan Ping (藍蘋), who plays the role of Nora, is a star in the Peking drama circle. She recently came south to join Dian Tong (電通). Although she is extremely busy filming, she still works hard to rehearse "Nora" every day. Ms. Wu Mei (吳湄), who plays the role of Lin Dun (林敦), is a veteran on the Shanghai stage. Ms. Han Mansong (韓曼松), who plays the role of Anna (阿納), is an unparalleled old female impersonator. Even the role of Irene (愛蘭) is played by Ms. Wu Ling (吳玲), the main actress of "Zhi Kuang (旨狂)". It can be seen how careful the selection of the actors for this "Nora" is.

Stage Personnel Engaged in Archaeology

For this performance, the stage set and lighting costumes are all in the style of the 19th century. For the sake of caution, many stage workers and costume designers have buried themselves in archaeology. It is said that this time, costumes alone have cost more than two hundred yuan.

Interlude from "Autumn Fan Bright Lamp (秋扇明燈)" 249

You Are My Lifeline

You are my lifeline—

Entrusting my great hope,

Maintaining my passionate heartstrings.

Let us always love each other!

Regardless of the fickleness of human affairs,

Let the world change like the sea,

As long as our hearts are as solid as gold,

What if we suffer hardship and poverty?

Cherish the fleeting years like water,

Do not take life lightly!

You are my lifeline.
